<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:barbershop.html>barbershop</a> (109377)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">barber</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">shop</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:barbershop.html>barbershop</a></strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">barbershops</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">countable</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The place of business of a barber; a store where a person (usually a <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a>) can go to get a haircut.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">uncountable<span class="ib-comma">,</span> music</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A style of a <a href = vnd.unilang:capella.html>capella</a> vocal music, sung in four-part harmony, typically by a quartet of <a href = vnd.unilang:men.html>men</a>.</li></ol>
</body>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:bardi.html>bardi</a> (109374)</h1><br></body> 
***bardo.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a> (77239)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BardoThodolChenmo.jpg/220px-BardoThodolChenmo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BardoThodolChenmo.jpg/330px-BardoThodolChenmo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/BardoThodolChenmo.jpg/440px-BardoThodolChenmo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="497" data-file-height="427" />  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"></div>Folios 35 and 67 of a manuscript of the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bardo_Thodol" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Bardo Thodol"><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>Bardo</a> Thodol</a></i> (<i>Liberation through Hearing during the Intermediate State</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup> often known in the West as the <i>Tibetan Book of the Dead</i>. The text <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> intended as a guide through the after-death experiences that a person’s consciousness <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> in the <a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_Tibetan" class="extiw" title="w:Standard Tibetan">Tibetan</a></span> <i class="Tibt mention" lang="bo">བར་དོ</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="bo-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn"><a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a> do</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <i class="Tibt mention" lang="bo">བར</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="bo-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn"><a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a></span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">interval</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + <i class="Tibt mention" lang="bo">དོ</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="bo-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">do</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">two</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-2"> | 2 | </a></sup> in the sense of an interval between two states.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">bardos</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">Tibetan  Buddhism</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The state of existence between death and subsequent reincarnation.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1863</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emil_Schlagintweit" class="extiw" title="w:Emil Schlagintweit">Emil Schlagintweit</a>,  “Details Characteristic of the Religion of the People”, in  <cite>Buddhism in Tibet: Illustrated by Literary Documents and <a href = vnd.unilang:objects.html>Objects</a> of Religious Worship. With an Account of the Buddhist Systems Preceding It in India. <span style="font-style: normal;">[...]</span> With a Folio Atlas of Twenty Plates and Twenty Tables of Native Print in the Text</cite>, Leipzig |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F.A._Brockhaus_AG" class="extiw" title="w:F.A. Brockhaus AG">F. A. Brockhaus</a>; London: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_Tr%C3%BCbner" class="extiw" title="w:Nicholas Trübner">Trübner amp; Co.</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/4233749">4233749</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=xrsIAAAAQAAJamp;pg=PA109">page 109</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:according.html>According</a> to the belief of the Tibetans, that <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> considered an untimely death, which, in opposition to the ordinary course of nature, <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> accelerated by evil <a href = vnd.unilang:spirits.html>spirits</a>, such as Sringan, Dechad, Jungpo, and others. As a consequence of premature decease, the "<b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>Bardo</a></b>," <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> prolongated. This <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the middle state between the death and the new re-birth, which does not follow immediately, but there exists an interval, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> shorter for the good than for the bad. The prolongation of this intermediate state <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> considered as a punishment caused by evil <a href = vnd.unilang:spirits.html>spirits</a> who have only power <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> sinful <a href = vnd.unilang:men.html>men</a>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1996</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victoria_LePage" class="extiw" title="w:Victoria LePage">Victoria LePage</a>,  “The Perfection of the Shortest Path”, in  <cite>Shambhala: The Fascinating Truth behind the Myth of Shangri-La</cite>, 1st Quest edition, Wheaton, Ill. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theosophical_Society_in_America" class="extiw" title="w:Theosophical Society in America">The Theosophical Publishing House</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=jV1bBgAAQBAJamp;pg=PA95">page 95</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The soul's gradual progress to <a href = vnd.unilang:god.html>God</a> in <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a> of a spiralling pathway up the side of the cosmic mountain, from one spiritual station to the next, <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> an image common to almost all of the world's mystical systems; but few mention the direct path from the base of the mountain straight up to the summit. <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>Even</a> the <a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>Bardo</a> Thodol mentions the direct path only once, and then glancingly, confining itself solely to a description of the soul's circuitous afterlife journey through the heaven-worlds. The shortcut for <a href = vnd.unilang:heroes.html>heroes</a> that bypasses the heaven-worlds or <b>bardos</b> and <a href = vnd.unilang:takes.html>takes</a> them straight to the divine world—in one lifetime, so it <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> said—is so well guarded in religious literature that the relevant Tibetan Buddhist texts are written in the "twilight language," a cipher that can be understood only with the help of revelation.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1998</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Susanne_Antonetta" class="extiw" title="w:Susanne Antonetta">Susanne <a href = vnd.unilang:paolo.html>Paolo</a></a>,  “Prologue”, in  <cite><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>Bardo</a></cite> (The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brittingham_Prize_in_Poetry" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Brittingham Prize in Poetry">Brittingham Prize in Poetry</a>), Madison, <a href = vnd.unilang:wis.html>Wis</a>. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:University of Wisconsin Press">University of Wisconsin Press</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=94EUTSs3owUCamp;pg=PR13">page xiii</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></b> in Tibetan means an intermediate state, most specifically the one after death when your soul wanders through the heavens and hell, trying to avoid rebirth into samsara—the realm of the material—and achieve nirvana or Buddhahood. <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> Like everything the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></b> journey <a href = vnd.unilang:takes.html>takes</a> place both inside you and outside. Like everything it's both a metaphor and not. I <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> born in the fifties in a nation suspended in the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></b> state between a war a decade <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> and the hellsmoke light of a new war pulling in the East.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2014</b>,  C. J. <a href = vnd.unilang:cala.html>Cala</a>,  “Babble On”, in  <cite>Four Different <a href = vnd.unilang:faces.html>Faces</a></cite>, [s.l.] |  C. J. <a href = vnd.unilang:cala.html>Cala</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=w7AtBAAAQBAJamp;pg=PA151">page 151</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Possessing both omniprescence and omniscience, they now stared beyond the abyss of astral space—beyond the six <b>bardos</b> of Tibetan Buddhism—spreading their karmic seeds across the infinite coordinates of the cosmological Minkowski continuum.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evan_Thompson" class="extiw" title="w:Evan Thompson"><a href = vnd.unilang:evan.html>Evan</a> Thompson</a>,  “Dying: What <a href = vnd.unilang:happens.html>Happens</a> when <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>We</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:die.html>Die</a>?”, in  <cite>Waking, Dreaming, Being: Self and Consciousness in Neuroscience, Meditation, and Philosophy</cite>, New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_University_Press" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Columbia University Press">Columbia University Press</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=q_vpBAAAQBAJamp;pg=PA292">page 292</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">"<b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>Bardo</a></b>," as noted, means in-between state. So whenever <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a>'re in between two states, no matter what the scale, <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a>'re in a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></b> state. These two states could be living and dying or being awake and being asleep, but they could also be the just-past <a href = vnd.unilang:moment.html>moment</a> of thought and the <a href = vnd.unilang:moment.html>moment</a> to come. Thus "<b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></b>" includes the gap between the cessation of one <a href = vnd.unilang:moment.html>moment</a> of thought and the arising of the next <a href = vnd.unilang:moment.html>moment</a>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b> January,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Jarboe_Russell" class="extiw" title="w:Jan Jarboe Russell">Jan Jarboe Russell</a>,  “The All-American Camp”, in  <cite>The Train to Crystal City: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" class="extiw" title="w:Franklin D. Roosevelt">FDR</a>’s Secret Prisoner Exchange Program and America’s only Family Internment Camp during World War II</cite>, New York, N.Y. |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Scribner%27s_Sons" class="extiw" title="w:Charles Scribner | s Sons">Scribner</a>, <small>→ISBN</small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=jE4tBgAAQBAJamp;pg=PA233">page 233</a>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">For internees the war <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> experienced in exile. The Buddhists in Crystal City understood it as a <i><b><a href = vnd.unilang:bardo.html>bardo</a></b></i> state—a provisional period between the <a href = vnd.unilang:lives.html>lives</a> before their confinement, and the dream of freedom after the war.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
</body>

***baren.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:baren.html>baren</a> (9574)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:baren.html>baren</a></i>. The <i>a</i> in the <a href = vnd.unilang:stem.html>stem</a> and the weak inflection are unetymological, but their origin <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> unknown. The form developed from and displaced the older strong <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:beren.html>beren</a></i> (still found in modern <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ontberen.html>ontberen</a></i>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">beran</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*beraną</i>. Ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*bʰer-</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:baren.html>baren</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to bear, to give birth to
<ul><li><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zij.html>Zij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:heeft.html>heeft</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>een</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zoon.html>zoon</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:gebaard.html>gebaard</a></b>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">She <a href = vnd.unilang:has.html>has</a> <b>borne</b> a son.</span></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to cause, to bring about
<ul><li><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dit.html>Dit</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:baart.html>baart</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zorgen.html>zorgen</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">This <b>causes</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> worry.</span></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:barnsteen.html>barnsteen</a> (71082)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">barn</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">burn</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:steen.html>steen</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">stone</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. The former part of the compound <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> related to the Dutch verb <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:branden.html>branden</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to burn</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:brimstone.html>brimstone</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Bernstein</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:amber.html>amber</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Icelandic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Icelandic language">Icelandic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="is">brennisteinn</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">sulfur, <a href = vnd.unilang:brimstone.html>brimstone</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>

***baron.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:baron.html>baron</a> (5741)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Readjustment from earlier <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">baroen</i> through French influence, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">baroen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro"><a href = vnd.unilang:baron.html>baron</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frankish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Frankish language">Frankish</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro">*baro</i>.

***barre.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:barre.html>barre</a> (25039)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_French" class="extiw" title="w:Middle French">Middle French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="frm"><a href = vnd.unilang:barre.html>barre</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro"><a href = vnd.unilang:barre.html>barre</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">beam, <a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a>, gate, barrier</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">*barra</i>, of uncertain origin. Perhaps from Old <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frankish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Frankish language">Frankish</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro">*bara</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a>, beam, barrier, fence</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*barō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">beam, <a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a>, barrier</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from  <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*BʰerH-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to strike, pierce</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. If so, then cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">para</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">bara</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a>, beam, one's cherished <a href = vnd.unilang:land.html>land</a></span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">bāre</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:baer.html>baer</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a>, barrier, rail</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Frisian" class="extiw" title="w:Old Frisian">Old Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ofs"><a href = vnd.unilang:ber.html>ber</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">attack, assault</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">bärling</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norwegian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Norwegian language">Norwegian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="no">berling</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">a small <a href = vnd.unilang:bar.html>bar</a> in a vehicle, rod</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span </p><p>An alternative etymology derives <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro"><a href = vnd.unilang:barre.html>barre</a></i> and <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">*barra</i> from a <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtic_languages" class="extiw" title="w:Celtic languages">Celtic</a></span> source related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breton_language" class="extiw" title="w:Breton language"><a href = vnd.unilang:breton.html>Breton</a></a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="br">barri</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">branch, twig</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.

***barse.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:barse.html>barse</a> (119602)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href = vnd.unilang:bars.html>bars</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">bærs</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">a fish, perch</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*barsaz</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">perch</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span>, literally <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">prickly</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:baars.html>baars</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">perch, bass</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Barsch</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">perch</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:barse.html>barse</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">barses</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>The perch; any of various marine and freshwater fish resembling the perch.</li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_terms">Related <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Blend of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:balls.html>balls</a></i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:arse.html>arse</a></i>.
</p>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:barst.html>barst</a> (4176)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:barst.html>barst</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="feminine gender">f</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:barst.html>barstje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>A crack, rip, tear</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">figuratively</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A little, a tiny amount; notably in: <i><a href = vnd.unilang:geen.html>geen</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:barst.html>barst</a></b> ("not a bit")</i></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> An outburst, eruption</li></ol>

***barsten.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a> (6517)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">bersten</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a></i>, from metathesis of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">brestan</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*brestaną</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*bʰres-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to burst, break, crack, split, separate</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to burst, split completely</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to crack, break partially
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>Het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ijs.html>ijs</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:begint.html>begint</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hier.html>hier</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:en.html>en</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:daar.html>daar</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a></b>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">The ice <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> starting to <b>crack up</b> in <a href = vnd.unilang:places.html>places</a>.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to <a href = vnd.unilang:suf.html>suffer</a> and/or break under emotional pressure</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To urge, be near emotional eruption
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:staat.html>staat</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:op.html>op</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:barsten.html>barsten</a></b>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">He's about to <b>explode</b>.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> basic (696)</h1><br></body> 
***basil.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:basil.html>basil</a> (12714)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1_2">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bacil.html>bacil</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">bacille</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Bazillus</i> or <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translingualism" class="extiw" title="w:Translingualism">translingual</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="mul"><i>Bacillus</i></i>, coined by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Gottfried_Ehrenberg" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Christian Gottfried Ehrenberg">Christian Gottfried Ehrenberg</a>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_4">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="id"><a href = vnd.unilang:basil.html>basil</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>bacillus</li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:basilicum.html>basilicum</a> (30070)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la"><a href = vnd.unilang:basilicum.html>basilicum</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">royal robe</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, substantive of <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">basilicus</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">royal, princely</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">βασιλικός</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">basilikós</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">royal</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:basilicum.html>basilicum</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:basilicum.html>basilicums</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:basilicum.html>basilicumpje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li><a href = vnd.unilang:basil.html>basil</a>, name of some plants of the mint family, notably:
<ol><li><i>Ocimum <a href = vnd.unilang:basilicum.html>basilicum</a></i>, an ornamental plant</li>
<li><span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Ocimum_suave" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Ocimum suave"><i>Ocimum suave</i></a></span>, cultivated for cookery</li></ol></li>
<li>the second plant's edible leaves, used as a spice</li>
<li>an ointment made from the plant</li></ol>

***bask.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:bask.html>bask</a> (52409)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Norse" class="extiw" title="w:Old Norse">Old <a href = vnd.unilang:norse.html>Norse</a></a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="non">baðask</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to take a bath</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span>, literally <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to bathe oneself</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, mediopassive form from underlying <i class="Latn mention" lang="non">baða</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to bathe</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + <i class="Latn mention" lang="non"><a href = vnd.unilang:sik.html>sik</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">oneself</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*baþōną</i> and <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sek</i>. Doublet of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">bathe</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:bask.html>bask</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">basks</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">basking</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">basked</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>To bathe in warmth; to be exposed to pleasant heat.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bask.html>bask</a></b> in the sun</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>1764</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oliver_Goldsmith" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Oliver Goldsmith"><a href = vnd.unilang:oliver.html>Oliver</a> Goldsmith</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Traveller_(poem)" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Traveller (poem)">The Traveller</a></i>
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> <b>basks</b> in the glare, and stems the tepid wave.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">figurative</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To take great pleasure or satisfaction; to feel warmth or happiness. (This verb <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> usually followed by "in").
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">I <b>basked</b> in her love.</i></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bask.html>bask</a></b> in someone's favour</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2012</b> November 7,  <a href = vnd.unilang:matt.html>Matt</a> Bai,  “Winning a Second Term, Obama Will Confront Familiar Headwinds”, in  <cite>New York Times</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/07/us/politics/in-president-obamas-second-term-familiar-challenges.html?pagewanted=allamp;_r=0">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">As President Obama turns his attention once again to filling out a cabinet and writing an Inaugural Address, this much <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> clear: he should not expect to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bask.html>bask</a></b> in a surge of national unity, or to witness a crowd of millions overrun the Mall just to say they <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> there.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2011</b> April 10,  Alistair Magowan,  “Aston <a href = vnd.unilang:villa.html>Villa</a> 1 <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> 0 Newcastle”, in  <cite>BBC Sport</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/sport2/hi/football/eng_prem/9446263.stm">[2]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">On this evidence they will certainly face tougher <a href = vnd.unilang:tests.html>tests</a>, as a depleted Newcastle side seemed to <b><a href = vnd.unilang:bask.html>bask</a></b> in the relative security of being ninth in the table</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>

***bassen.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:bassen.html>bassen</a> (45862)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:bassen.html>bassen</a></i>, probably onomatopoeic. Further etymology <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> unknown, there are no known cognates.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bassen.html>bassen</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to bark, like a dog (rarely in the sense of shouting)</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to produce a somewhat similar sound, notably as result of a cough</li></ol>

<p>See the etymology of the main entry.

***bastaard.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:bastaard.html>bastaard</a> (6154)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">bastaert</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">bastard</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastaard.html>bastaard</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastaarden.html>bastaarden</a></b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastaards.html>bastaards</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastaardje.html>bastaardje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>A bastard, person born to unmarried parents; in some legal systems a non-heir, or on that <a href = vnd.unilang:criterium.html>criterium</a> restricted to illegitimate sons</li>
<li>An animal or plant genetically 'degenerated' by having parents of different species or <a href = vnd.unilang:races.html>races</a></li>
<li>A bastardised term or language</li></ol>

***bastille.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:bastille.html>bastille</a> (36321)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastille.html>bastille</a></i>, from <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Late Latin">Late Latin</a></span></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">bastilia</i>, plural of <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">bastile</i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">bastire</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to build</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastille.html>bastille</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">bastilles</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A castle tower, or fortified building; a small citadel or fortress.</li>
<li>A prison or jail.
<ul><li><b>1663</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Butler" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Samuel Butler">Samuel <a href = vnd.unilang:butler.html>Butler</a></a>, <i>Hudibras</i>, I.2:
<dl><dd>Thither arriv'd, th' advent'rous Knight / And bold Squire from their <a href = vnd.unilang:steeds.html>Steeds</a> alight, / At th' outward Wall, near which there <a href = vnd.unilang:stands.html>stands</a> / A <b>Bastile</b>, built <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a>' imprison Hands [...].</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:bastille.html>bastille</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">bastilles</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">bastilling</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">bastilled</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>To confine as though in a <a href = vnd.unilang:bastille.html>bastille</a>; to imprison.
<ul><li><b>1796–7</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Wollstonecraft" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Mary Wollstonecraft"><a href = vnd.unilang:mary.html>Mary</a> Wollstonecraft</a>, <i>The Wrongs of Woman</i>, Oxford 2009, p. 137:
<dl><dd>Marriage <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> <b>bastilled</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:me.html>me</a> for life.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
</body>

***baten.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:baten.html>baten</a> (37409)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum"><a href = vnd.unilang:baten.html>baten</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*baton</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*batāną</i>, from the same root as <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:beter.html>beter</a></i>.
